1. **Content Creation**: Develop clear, engaging, and technically accurate content for web-based presentations and project documentation, ensuring alignment with project goals and user needs.
   
2. **Event Leadership**: Lead and deliver presentations during team meetings and external events, communicating complex technical topics in an accessible manner to varied audiences.

3. **Project Management**: Oversee the planning, development, and execution of web projects, ensuring all technical and design elements meet project objectives and deadlines.

4. **Feedback Integration**: Actively incorporate feedback from team members, stakeholders, and clients to continuously improve both the technical and creative aspects of web projects.

5. **Trend Awareness**: Stay informed about the latest web development trends, frameworks, and tools, sharing insights with the team to maintain cutting-edge web experiences.

6. **Innovation and Ideation**: Lead brainstorming sessions to generate innovative ideas for web projects, and contribute solutions that push the boundaries of technical capabilities and user experience.

7. **Project Ownership**: Take full accountability for the success of all web projects, ensuring timely delivery, functionality, and adherence to industry best practices.

8. **Adaptability**: Demonstrate flexibility by managing various technical tasks, from frontend and backend development to performance optimization and web security within different project contexts.

This agreement serves as a Memorandum of Understanding (MoU) between the participants of the GDG on Campus MAKAUT GenAI Campaign and the event organizers. 09/12/24, 11:17 - Nirvik Ghosh: Here‚Äôs a detailed speech script to guide you through your 4-hour session on "Intro to Python Programming" with humor and engaging content.


---

Introduction (15 minutes)

[Slide 1: Welcome]
Speech:
‚ÄúGood morning, everyone! I‚Äôm Nirvik Ghosh, aka the Django Wizard üêç, and alongside me is Aditya Ghosh, aka Tony Stark (without the Arc Reactor, unfortunately). Together, we‚Äôre here to guide you through the magical world of Python programming.

Let me start with a question: How many of you have coded before? And how many are here because your manager said, ‚ÄòLearn Python or else‚Äô? Don‚Äôt worry; whether you‚Äôre a seasoned coder or a reluctant learner, this session has something for everyone.‚Äù

Humor:
‚ÄúYou‚Äôll soon realize Python is like your best friend‚Äîfun to hang out with and never judgmental about how many times you mess up.‚Äù

Icebreaker:
"Let's start with expectations. Write down or shout out what you want to learn today. My favorite so far: ‚ÄòLearn Python faster than my cat can destroy my keyboard.‚Äô Challenge accepted!"


---

Session 1: Programming Basics (45 minutes)

[Slide 2: What is Programming?]
Speech:
‚ÄúProgramming is a way to make computers work for you‚Äîbasically, turning coffee into code. It‚Äôs like magic but with more debugging. Let me put it another way: If your phone can play your favorite meme compilation at 2 a.m., thank a programmer.‚Äù

Meme on Screen: ‚ÄòWhy do programmers prefer dark mode? Because light attracts bugs.‚Äô

Explain:
‚ÄúProgramming boils down to three key steps:

1. You tell the computer what to do.


2. It follows your instructions.


3. And then it shows you exactly how wrong you were. But that‚Äôs okay‚Äîwe learn from our errors.‚Äù




---

[Slide 3: Hello, World!]
Demo:
‚ÄúLet‚Äôs start with every programmer‚Äôs rite of passage‚Äîprinting Hello, World! in Python. Here‚Äôs how it‚Äôs done:

print("Hello, World!")

See how clean and simple that is? If this were C, you‚Äôd be writing twice the lines just to say hello.‚Äù

Humor:
‚ÄúPython is like that one friend who keeps things chill. Other languages? Not so much.‚Äù


---

Session 2: Python Foundations (1 hour)

[Slide 4: Variables and Data Types]
Speech:
‚ÄúVariables are like Tupperware for your data‚Äîyou can store stuff, retrieve it later, and sometimes forget what you put in. For example:

x = 42
print(x)

This creates a variable x and stores the number 42 in it. You can change it later to something else‚Äîlike your mood when your code finally runs!‚Äù

Meme on Screen: ‚ÄòWhen you fix one bug, but three more show up: Hydra from Marvel.‚Äô


---

[Slide 5: Numbers and Strings]
Speech:
‚ÄúNumbers are for math. Strings? They‚Äôre for making things fun. Strings are just text, like this:

name = "Python"
print("I love " + name)

You can even multiply strings:

print("Python! " * 3)
# Output: Python! Python! Python!

Who needs a therapist when you can have Python hype you up?‚Äù


---

Lunch Break (1 Hour)
Speech:
‚ÄúYou‚Äôve worked hard, and now it‚Äôs time to recharge. Enjoy your lunch, and when we come back, we‚Äôll tackle the most exciting part‚Äîmaking decisions and repeating tasks. Also, I‚Äôve set up a meme slideshow to keep you entertained while you eat. See you in an hour!‚Äù


---

Session 3: Control Flow (1 Hour)

[Slide 6: Conditionals]
Speech:
‚ÄúConditionals help your program make decisions. It‚Äôs like life: If hungry, then eat. Let‚Äôs write this in Python:

hungry = True
if hungry:
    print("Let‚Äôs grab food!")

Pretty straightforward, right? Let‚Äôs try something fun:

age = 18
if age < 21:
    print("Teenager")
else:
    print("Adult")

Now try modifying the age variable and see what happens.‚Äù

Meme on Screen: ‚ÄòIf debugging is the process of removing bugs, then programming must be the process of putting them in.‚Äô


---

[Slide 7: Loops]
Speech:
‚ÄúLoops are for tasks you need to repeat‚Äîlike reminding your team to update their code. For example:

for i in range(5):
    print("Don‚Äôt forget to commit your changes!")

This prints the message five times. Now let‚Äôs try a while loop:

count = 0
while count < 3:
    print("Learning Python is fun!")
    count += 1

Pro tip: Be careful with loops; an infinite loop can make your computer scream for mercy.‚Äù


---

Session 4: Advanced Topics (1 Hour)

[Slide 8: Functions]
Speech:
‚ÄúFunctions are like recipes. They let you reuse code and keep things organized. Let‚Äôs create a simple function:

def greet(name):
    return f"Hello, {name}!"
print(greet("World"))

See how neat that is? Functions save time and reduce errors.‚Äù


---

[Slide 9: Collections and Modules]
Speech:
‚ÄúCollections are like your shopping list‚Äîyou group related items together. For example:

fruits = ["apple", "banana", "cherry"]
for fruit in fruits:
    print(fruit)

Modules are like pre-packed tools for your code. You can import them and use their functions. For example, the math module lets you do this:

import math
print(math.sqrt(16))  # Output: 4.0

Python‚Äôs standard library is a treasure trove of useful modules.‚Äù


---

Conclusion (15 Minutes)

[Slide 10: Recap and Q&A]
Speech:
‚ÄúTo wrap up, let‚Äôs review what we learned today:

1. Python basics‚Äîvariables, numbers, and strings.


2. Decision-making with conditionals.


3. Repeating tasks with loops.


4. Organizing code with functions and collections.



Q&A Session:
‚ÄúNow it‚Äôs your turn! Got questions? Hit me with your toughest ones‚Äîexcept for, ‚ÄòWhy isn‚Äôt my code working?‚Äô That‚Äôs everyone‚Äôs mystery.‚Äù

Closing Joke:
‚ÄúThank you for joining us today! Remember, programming is 90% Googling and 10% actual coding. So if you leave here confused, just blame Stack Overflow.‚Äù


---

Would you like additional memes or specific exercises for the attendees?

30/01/25, 01:03 - Nirvik Ghosh: **GDSC MAKAUT Event Report 2023-24**  
*Empowering Students Through Technology and Innovation*  

The Google Developer Student Club (GDSC) at Maulana Abul Kalam Azad University of Technology (MAKAUT) has been at the forefront of fostering technical excellence, innovation, and collaboration among students. The academic year 2023-24 witnessed a series of impactful events, workshops, and initiatives aimed at equipping students with cutting-edge skills and knowledge in various domains of technology. Here‚Äôs a detailed report of the key events organized by GDSC MAKAUT during this period.  

---

### **GDSC MAKAUT Info Session 1.0**  
**Date:** 28th August 2023  
**Speaker:** Avik Mukherjee  
**Guest Speakers:**  
- Dr. Sibamay Dasgupta, Professor of IT  
- Dr. Debashis De, Professor of CSE  
- Dr. Prodip Mukherjee  
- Mr. Joy Samadder  

**Objectives:**  
- **Knowledge Sharing:** Enhancing technical skills and learning about Google services.  
- **Networking:** Connecting with like-minded individuals.  
- **Problem Solving:** Collaborating on real-world tech projects.  
- **Hands-on Projects:** Focusing on practical learning.  
- **Open Source:** Encouraging contributions to open-source projects.  
- **Continuous Growth:** Providing resources for ongoing learning.  
- **Workshops & Events:** Conducting sessions on Web Development, Cloud, AI/ML, Android, Flutter, and Git/GitHub.  
- **Hackathons:** Organizing competitions to foster creativity.  
- **Skill Development:** Improving technical, teamwork, and management skills.  
- **Inclusive Community:** Building a collaborative and friendly ecosystem.  

The session set the tone for the year, inspiring students to actively participate in GDSC activities and leverage the opportunities provided by the club.  

---

### **Open Source Unleashed: A Journey into GitHub**  
**Date:** 4th November 2023  
**Speaker:** Avik Mukherjee  
**Guest Speaker:** Sayak Saha (Systems Engineer @ TCS Digital)  

**Objectives:**  
- Understanding the game-changing impact of Open Source.  
- Learning collaboration etiquette.  
- Starting contributions at any skill level.  
- Drawing inspiration from success stories.  
- Mastering GitHub as the ultimate open-source hub.  
- Participating in a hands-on workshop.  

This event demystified the world of open-source contributions and encouraged students to actively participate in global projects using GitHub.  

---

### **Flutter Fiesta 2023-24**  
**Date:** 25th March 2023  
**Speaker:** Avik Mukherjee  
**Guest Speaker:** Tanmoy Karmakar (SDE-III @ Tide)  

**Objectives:**  
- Understanding Flutter and its advantages/disadvantages.  
- Building the first app using Flutter (hands-on session).  

The workshop provided students with practical exposure to Flutter, enabling them to create their first mobile applications.  

---

### **Google Cloud Study Jam Swag Distribution Ceremony 2023-24**  
**Date:** 25th March 2024  
**Speaker:** Avik Mukherjee  
**Guest Speakers:**  
- Dr. Tapash Chakraborty, VC, MAKAUT, WB  
- Dr. Partha Pratim Lahiri, Registrar, MAKAUT, WB  
- Dr. Atri Bhowmick, Finance Officer, MAKAUT, WB  
- Dr. Md Aftabuddin, Information Scientist, MAKAUT, WB  
- Mr. Joy Samadder  

**Objective:**  
Celebrating the achievements of students who completed their Google Cloud Lab assessments, the ceremony awarded exclusive Google Cloud swags to the first 60 participants. The event coincided with National Science Day, adding a touch of pride and inspiration.  

**Insights:**  
- 60 students were awarded Google Cloud swags.  
- The event highlighted the importance of cloud computing skills in today‚Äôs tech-driven world.  

---

### **AIML Workshop 2023-24: AI and ML Unleashed ‚Äì Navigating the Future**  
**Date:** 16th‚Äì17th May 2024  
**Speakers:**  
- Indraneel Sarkar  
- Suchintika Sarkar  
- Soumyadeep Ganguly  
- Sugata Ray Chaudhary  
- Debashis Bera  
- Mayank Raj  
- Ishita Majhi  

**Objectives:**  
The workshop aimed to provide students with a comprehensive understanding of Artificial Intelligence (AI) and Machine Learning (ML). It covered foundational concepts, practical applications, and future trends, catering to both beginners and advanced learners.  

**Topics Covered:**  
- Basic Mathematics of Machine Learning  
- Numpy & Pandas  
- Data Gathering and Web Scraping  
- Regression Models  
- Classification Models  
- Introduction to Deep Learning  

**Projects Made:**  
- Regression  
- Classification  

**Insights:**  
- Students learned the basics of Machine Learning models.  
- Hands-on projects on Regression and Classification were completed.  
- Web scraping and an introduction to Deep Learning were also covered.  

---

### **GDSC MAKAUT Campaign 2023-24**  
Throughout the year, GDSC MAKAUT organized several campaigns and initiatives to promote technical learning and innovation:  

1. **Google Cloud Study Jam 2023-24**  
   - Facilitator: Ritam Mishra  
   - Focused on cloud computing skills and hands-on labs.  

2. **GDSC Solution Challenge 2024**  
   - Encouraged students to develop solutions for real-world problems using Google technologies.  

3. **GenAI Study Jam 2023-24**  
   - Introduced students to Generative AI and its applications.  

---

### **Conclusion**  
The 2023-24 academic year was a remarkable journey for GDSC MAKAUT, marked by a series of successful events, workshops, and campaigns. These initiatives not only enhanced the technical skills of students but also fostered a spirit of collaboration, innovation, and continuous learning. 28/03/25, 20:32 - Nirvik Ghosh: Akshit Jain welcomed participants to the facilitator onboarding session, explaining its purpose: to equip facilitators with the necessary information to promote Google Cloud Skills Boost Arcade and help users begin cloud computing careers. Jain outlined the session's structure‚Äîprimarily a one-way information sharing session followed by a Q&A‚Äîand emphasized the importance of team partner participation, using the Q&A feature for questions, and noting that the session was being recorded. Jain also mentioned some logistical aspects of the meeting such as keeping oneself muted and requesting a quick thumbs-up/thumbs-down to check for audio issues.
Akshit Jain shared information regarding the session recording and a publicly accessible deck containing mostly confidential information, emphasizing the importance of non-disclosure and the consequences of sharing it. Jain also explained the team disqualification policy and introduced the program managers involved: Jain (a program manager at Google Cloud), Yugali Mohite (program manager for the Google Cloud Skills Boost Arcade program), and Reta (another program manager). Yugali Mohite then briefly introduced herself and thanked the facilitators for their contributions to the program's success.
Akshit Jain expressed appreciation for Yuggali's YouTube videos and introduced Rutuja Vilas Yerunkar, a new team member. Akshit Jain then outlined the upcoming kickoff session, detailing its 1.5-hour duration, focus on user enrollment and completion tracking in the Google Cloud Skills Boost program, and coverage of facilitator badges, website features, progress tracking, and engagement tips. The session aims to equip facilitators with the tools to successfully guide users and includes revisiting program details, timelines, prizes, and resources.
Akshit Jain explained the Arcade Facilitator program, highlighting its expansion to include Google Cloud Lab free courses alongside the existing skills boost arcade games, trivia games, and Google Cloud skill badges. Jain emphasized that all games, including newly added titles like Arcade Base Camp and Certification Zone, now contribute to user milestones, rewarding participant time investment and fostering a collaborative, non-competitive environment among facilitators. The program aims to provide facilitators with detailed program information, recognize their efforts with rewards and certificates, and help them develop skills in community management and leadership.
Akshit Jain explained the Google Cloud Skills Boost facilitator program, highlighting new lab limits implemented to prevent platform abuse and the introduction of lab-free courses to ensure uninterrupted learning. Jain detailed the program schedule, emphasizing the crucial April-June period for driving user completions and achieving milestones, followed by reward distribution in June based on progress and the completion of at least 100 student enrollments. Jain concluded by outlining the facilitator milestone requirements, including driving 400 game completions and 1000 skill badge completions, emphasizing that rewards are given only for the highest milestone reached and that significant planning and research went into designing the program.
Akshit Jain detailed the prizes for achieving various milestones in the Arcade Facilitator program, including a Google certificate, a facilitator hoodie, a Lego diary, a motion light, and a Google Cloud Edison bulb, with additional prizes such as a power bank and an "ultimate swag" item to be revealed later. Jain also clarified that completing facilitator milestones doesn't automatically grant users the corresponding player achievements in the Skills Boost Arcade program, emphasizing the program's purpose is to encourage user-led learning and exploration.
Akshit Jain outlined the user milestones, which involve completing arcade and trivia games, skill badges, and provided lab-free courses, culminating in an ultimate milestone with significant rewards. Jain emphasized that while the program offers attractive incentives like swags and certificates to enhance resumes, the primary focus should be on skill development and career advancement. Jain also announced a mandatory facilitator badge, accessible via a provided link and access code, with a deadline of June 2nd, emphasizing its compulsory nature for all facilitators to receive prizes.
Akshit Jain emphasized the importance of completing a task promptly to be eligible for prizes and certificates, then guided participants through the Arcade Facilitator website, highlighting its features, upcoming program dates (April 1st to June 2nd), and crucial information for users. Jain also addressed potential issues with enrollment emails ending up in spam folders, advising participants to instruct users to add the Google Cloud email address to their contacts and ensure sufficient email storage, and to utilize referral codes carefully to avoid typos.
Akshit Jain discussed key aspects of the Arcade Facilitator program, including the 600-credit reward, a new "journey" section guiding users based on time commitment and milestones, and updated lab attempt limits (15 labs per 24 hours, with one attempt replenishing every two hours). Jain also highlighted the importance of the program's code of conduct, the availability of different game types throughout the month, and the distinction between facilitator milestones and kit pair achievements, emphasizing the need for clarity regarding these points for participants.
Akshit Jain described the architect facilitator program website, detailing its structured learning journeys (beginner, intermediate, advanced), each with specified durations and credit requirements, including breaks. Jain also highlighted key website sections: arcade and trivia game access updates, a public catalog organized by skill level (with 45 skill badges and 18 free courses), and a comprehensive FAQ page to minimize support inquiries, emphasizing the importance of reviewing the program's terms and conditions and code of conduct to avoid disqualification.
Akshit Jain introduced Yugali Mohite, who presented the Space Boost Arcade website, emphasizing the importance of user subscription with matching email IDs across platforms to avoid point discrepancies. Yugali Mohite detailed the website's features, including various games (like the "Zero Waste Infinite" game, which, though not part of the facilitator program, offers valuable skill-building and points), the point system (one point per game/trivia badge, one point per two skill badges), and the recently announced milestone tiers (20, 40, 65, 75, and 85 points).
Yugali Mohite announced early program details, emphasizing the importance of the Google Cloud Community as the primary source of information and the availability of email support due to the disabled chat function; Akshit Jain reiterated this, highlighting the distinction between the arcade facilitator program's point system and a new game not included in the program, and stressed the importance of user subscription to the arcade to ensure accurate point tracking, noting that milestone completion in the facilitator program does not guarantee arcade swag.
Akshit Jain discussed the facilitator program's point system, emphasizing that facilitators should not compete with or harass each other, and should focus on managing their own communities. Jain also detailed the importance of accurate referral codes for user enrollment and explained the upcoming daily progress reports, noting a delay in their start date until around April 6th or 8th to allow for enrollment processing. Finally, Jain highlighted the availability of facilitators' Google Cloud Community profiles for users to learn more about them.
Akshit Jain informed participants about upcoming reports containing user progress data, including lab-free course completion details and public profile URL status verification. Jain then outlined resources for engaging users, suggesting tools like Google Meet, YouTube live streams, and community platforms (WhatsApp, Discord, Slack, Telegram, Google Classroom, Google Cloud Zoom) to facilitate online sessions and knowledge sharing, emphasizing the importance of pre- and post-session work and providing links to helpful videos and promotional materials. Finally, Jain encouraged participants to utilize these resources to build their own communities and promote program participation through various social media channels.
Akshit Jain informed the facilitators about available resources, including banners, logos, pre-written messages, and email templates, emphasizing the importance of using email communication for professional user engagement and confidentiality of shared information. Jain also highlighted helpful external resources like a Google website with various tools and recommended tools such as SlideIcon, Canva, Easy GIF, Zapier, and App Script, advising facilitators to use the FAQ, Google Chat community, or email support for user queries, and encouraging a "Google it yourself" approach for problem-solving, promoting user self-reliance and improved developer skills.
Akshit Jain addressed questions regarding the Google Cloud Arcade Facilitator program, clarifying that participation does not include access to Google India events like Google IO or Devfest, nor does it include Google swag like Nest Mini or Nest Hub. Jain also explained that the program's lab completion limit is 15 labs per 24 hours this year, with a new lab attempt available every two hours, and that past badge completions will not count for new participants, though they can use their existing email IDs. Finally, Jain confirmed that facilitators can participate in the program for bonus points and that arcade points do not carry over between seasons.
Latest update
Akshit Jain addressed several questions regarding the program, including participant account usage (old accounts are acceptable, but users must be over 18), hoodie quality concerns (feedback noted, but a switch to White Scale is under consideration), and milestone rewards (both teammates receive swag upon completion, and rewards are detailed on the arcade website). Akshit Jain also clarified that only six games are part of the arcade facilitator program, and that using materials from previous kickoff decks is prohibited due to confidentiality, advising the use of publicly available website resources instead. Finally, Abishek's concern about unclear milestone rewards was addressed by Akshit Jain, who explained that arcade milestones offer swag, while arcade facilitator rewards bonus points, with details available on the arcade website.

31/03/25, 22:28 - Nirvik Ghosh: ESPRESSO MARTINI COCKTAIL
The espresso martini has been made hugely popular in recent years due to the addictive combination of coffee & vodka! Make sure you use cold drip coffee - coffee extracted with heat tends to go bitter when not used immediately. Cold drip makes a delicious and consistent Espresso Martini - every time!

30mL Coffee Liqueur (1 oz)
30mL Vodka (1 oz)
30mL Coffee (1 oz)

NEGRONI COCKTAIL
This cocktail resembles the Americano (minus the soda and replaced with gin). Not to everyone's taste though I must admit - try easing into one by replacing the Campari with a less bitter Italian aperitif, Aperol - yum!

30mL Gin (1 oz)
30mL Sweet Vermouth (1 oz)
30mL Campari (1 oz)

APEROL SPRITZ COCKTAIL
The Aperol Spritz is a popular summer drink! Aperol's grapefruit notes and subtle bitterness compliment the bubbly, sweeter style prosecco.

90mL Prosecco (3 oz)
60mL Aperol (2 oz)
30mL Soda Water (1 oz)
31/03/25, 22:28 - Nirvik Ghosh: BROWN DERBY COCKTAIL
The Brown Derby is somewhat of a bourbon whiskey based riff on a classic daiquiri. A big measure of bourbon is balanced with sweet honey syrup and sour and subtly bitter grapefruit juice. Named after the popular LA restaurant from the mid-20th century.

60mL Bourbon Whiskey (2 oz)
30mL Fresh Grapefruit Juice (1 oz)
15mL Honey Syrup (1:1) (¬Ω oz)

BEES KNEES COCKTAIL
The Bee's Knees cocktail recipe was invented out of necessity, hiding the poor quality homemade, bathtub cut gin that was prevalent during the prohibition-era. Nowadays, good quality gin is in abundance and this is a delicious, citrusy and honeyed gin cocktail.

60mL Gin (2 oz)
15mL Fresh Lemon Juice (¬Ω oz)
15mL Honey Syrup (1:1) (¬Ω oz)

MARGARITA COCKTAIL
Tequila and especially margaritas are party drinks, so instead of serving them up in a stemmed Margarita glass, serve them up short on ice by following this simple simple 3-2-1 recipe.

45mL Tequila (1¬Ω oz)
15mL Triple Sec (¬Ω oz)
30mL Fresh Lime Juice(1 oz)
31/03/25, 22:28 - Nirvik Ghosh: DAIQUIRI COCKTAIL
The Daiquiri would have to be one of the most iconic classics. It was first created in the 1890's and Bacardi was first call. Originally the drink was served in a tall glass packed with ice.

60mL White Rum (2 oz)
22.5mL Fresh Lime Juice (¬æ oz)
22.5mL Sugar Syrup (¬æ oz)

GODFATHER COCKTAIL
The original recipe of the Godfather calls for equal parts of Scotch Whisky and Amaretto which is quite sweet. I prefer to increase the Scotch Whisky to 45mL and drop the Amaretto to 15mL creating a less sweet and dryer Godfather recipe. Either way, the Amaretto will smooth and sweeten the whisky into a velvety smooth and tasty stirred drink.

45mL Scotch Whisky (1¬Ω oz)
15mL Amaretto (¬Ω oz)

MANHATTAN COCKTAIL
60mL Rye whisky (2 oz)
30mL Sweet Red Vermouth (1 oz)
2-3 Dashes of Bitters

BRANDY FLIP COCKTAIL
The Brandy Flip is a simple, 3-ingredient cocktail with a rich flavour and creamy texture. The very first Flips emerged as early as the late 1600s - they were originally created with a mixture of sugar, eggs and spices being added to a tankard of ale before being heated with a red-hot iron poker from the fire. Now, a Flip commonly refers to a cocktail of fortified wine or spirit and whole egg sweetened with sugar.

60mL Brandy (2 oz)
30mL Simple Syrup (1:1) (1 oz)
Whole Egg

04/04/25, 21:41 - Nirvik Ghosh: [READ CAREFULLY] Providing clarifications on the "Enrolment Form". sharing some Important guidelines & information and providing solutions to common problems ‚úÖ

Hey facilitators! I know many of you are having doubts and concerns regarding a lot of things and we are just here to offer clarifications and solutions so that you can help your users better. Please CAREFULLY READ all the information in this announcement below which should answer all of your queries above. üôÇ

First of all - NEVER PANIC! 
As facilitators, you carry a weight on your shoulders to keep your user communities calm and composed but at the same time, keep them posted about the rules and regulations of the program. Always assure them, that Google will uphold every piece of information that has been sent out about the program and if at some point there was a mistake from their end, then they will surely rectify it with appropriate measures! üòá

‚úîÔ∏è Clarifying Enrolment Form Closure
As you have already noticed, the enrolment form was closed today. Please note that this happened automatically as the system detected that we had reached our maximum number of seats in the program before the deadline of 10th April and thus the form closed automatically. Note that - this is CLEARLY mentioned on the site as well here under "Program Timeline" and if anyone is reaching out to you, then you should redirect them to the same rules. ‚è∞

‚úîÔ∏è Can we open the enrolment form again?
Unfortunately, the enrolment form cannot be opened again. We wish there was a way, but unfortunately, even our hands are tied here. Rules have been put in place to provide everyone a fair chance to participate and enrol. The form was open for almost 3.5 days which was more than enough time for each facilitator team to at-least enrol more than 100 users and this goes for every facilitator - facilitators who enrolled a 100 users and who didn't. This is NOT unfair at all and you should definitely help your users understand the importance of time and schedules. ‚òëÔ∏è

‚úîÔ∏è What happens to facilitators with less than 100 users?
We have decided that we will let the facilitators continue with the program as opposed to the eligibility criteria thus still keeping them hopeful that they can at-least reach any one of the facilitator milestones. We will also be making some changes in the user-facilitator mapping, especially for the one who submitted incorrect referral codes and will try our best to find a way we can equally promote all the facilitators having at least a 100 users. This way, both users and the facilitators will be able to benefit and continue with the program.

We completely understand that there was a misuse of the enrolment forms where fake entries were submitted. This is REALLY BAD and NOT something that we expect from our facilitators! ‚ùå We will surely investigate this further and take appropriate disciplinary actions.

‚úîÔ∏è How can the users updates their details now?
We will soon open a new "Updation Form" using which users will be able to correct their profile URLs. We will specifically gate this form behind a sign-in process so that only users who own those accounts will be able to make those changes and no one else. üí™

‚úîÔ∏è For users who are claiming that they DID NOT receive the enrolment email or DID NOT receive the credits
As we have already shared many times on both the topics, both of these things generally means that there is an issue from the users' end and not from Google's side, and they surely need to wait for 24-48 hours to receive the same. Despite that, please ask the users to reach out to the arcade-facilitator@google.com and our support team will help them with the same. 

Do ask them to BE PATIENT after dropping an email and wait for at least 3-4 days for a reply. Our support team is receiving a LOT of queries and they are trying their best to reply back to everyone. üôÇ
04/04/25, 21:42 - Nirvik Ghosh: ‚úîÔ∏èWhen will the daily reports start going out?
We generally would have already started the daily reports by today/tomorrow, but since the enrolments forms closed earlier than expected, we will now immediately go into the "validation checks" where any duplicate entries, any users with duplicate profile URLs OR anyone who has been incorrectly enrolled in the program and does not meet the eligibility criteria, will be REMOVED. Since, this process can take some time, your daily reports will start coming out from Monday, next week and will continue until the end of the program.

‚úîÔ∏è Meanwhile, NOT to worry, there will be a 2nd Cohort ü§©
We understand that the forms might have been closed earlier than expected and we also understand that this might have not given all the facilitators to enrol their users in the program OR reach a 100 seats. No need to worry, all of this cohort's facilitators will also get a chance to participate again in the next cohort that will be happening later this year and the same goes for the users as well. ‚úÖ Hence, we request you to please be patient and wait for the 2nd cohort to be launched!

And finally, a HUGE KUDOS to everyone. I think this was the first time our enrolment forms were closed this early and this fast. While right now it might be seeming a little bleak, note that this was an outstanding accomplishment and clearly speaks to the AMAZING facilitators that you are.

We hope you have a great journey ahead and please be patient to receive further updates from our end.

See you in the cloud,
Akshit & the Arcade Facilitator Team

06/04/25, 18:32 - Nirvik Ghosh: The Google Cloud Arcade Facilitator Program is a learning initiative where participants can explore Google Cloud technologies through hands-on labs and challenges. It‚Äôs designed for students, developers, and tech enthusiasts who want to gain practical cloud computing skills.

Why Should You Participate?

1. Learn by Doing ‚Äì Instead of just reading about cloud computing, you get to practice real-world tasks on Google Cloud.

# Load the image in color
image = cv2.imread('path_to_image.jpg')  # Replace with your image path
print("Original Image Shape (H, W, C):", image.shape)
print("Matrix Representation (BGR):")
print(image)

# Convert to Grayscale
gray = cv2.cvtColor(image, cv2.COLOR_BGR2GRAY)
print("Grayscale Image Shape:", gray.shape)
print("Matrix Representation (Grayscale):")
print(gray)

# Access pixel at (100, 100)
(b, g, r) = image[100, 100]
print(f"Pixel at (100, 100) - B: {b}, G: {g}, R: {r}")

# Thresholding (binary image)
_, thresh = cv2.threshold(gray, 127, 255, cv2.THRESH_BINARY)
print("Thresholded Image:")
print(thresh)

# Edge detection using Canny
edges = cv2.Canny(gray, 100, 200)
print("Edge-detected Image:")
print(edges)

import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Load the image in color (BGR format)
image = cv2.imread('path_to_image.jpg')  # Replace with your image path

# Convert BGR to RGB for correct display with matplotlib
image_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(image, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)

# Convert to Grayscale
gray = cv2.cvtColor(image, cv2.COLOR_BGR2GRAY)

# Thresholding
_, thresh = cv2.threshold(gray, 127, 255, cv2.THRESH_BINARY)

# Edge detection

‚úîÔ∏è Student Progress Reports will go out from TOMORROW üéä (Friday 11th April)

There will be 4 kinds of emails that will be sent out to the users based on where they are in their learning journey:

Email #2 - Email to help users redeem their access codes if they have NOT yet redeemed it and have ZERO badge completions.
Email #3 = Email to help users complete their first badge in the program if they have redeemed their access code but still have ZERO badge completions

20/04/25, 01:09 - Arpan Sinha BCA (1-) Junior: from flask import Flask, request, jsonify
from flask_cors import CORS
import os
import csv
from werkzeug.utils import secure_filename

app = Flask(__hmm__)
CORS(app)

UPLOAD_FOLDER = 'uploads'
ALLOWED_EXTENSIONS = {'csv'}
app.config['UPLOAD_FOLDER'] = UPLOAD_FOLDER

if not os.path.exists(UPLOAD_FOLDER):
    os.makedirs(UPLOAD_FOLDER)

def allowed_file(filename):
    return '.' in filename and filename.rsplit('.', 1)[1].lower() in ALLOWED_EXTENSIONS

@app.route('/upload', methods=['POST'])
def upload_csv():
    if 'file' not in request.files:
        return jsonify({'error': 'No file part'}), 400

    file = request.files['file']

    if file.filename == '':
        return jsonify({'error': 'No selected file'}), 400

    if file and allowed_file(file.filename):
        filename = secure_filename(file.filename)
        filepath = os.path.join(app.config['UPLOAD_FOLDER'], filename)
        file.save(filepath)

        leaderboard_data = []

        with open(filepath, newline='', encoding='utf-8') as csvfile:
            reader = csv.DictReader(csvfile)
            for row in reader:
                try:
                    arcade_games = int(row.get('Arcade Games', 0))
                    skill_badges = int(row.get('Skill Badges', 0))
                    trivia_games = int(row.get('Trivia Games', 0))
                    total_points = arcade_games + skill_badges + trivia_games
                    leaderboard_data.append({
                        'User Name': row['User Name'],
                        'Arcade Games': arcade_games,
                        'Skill Badges': skill_badges,
                        'Trivia Games': trivia_games,
                        'Total Points': total_points
                    })
                except Exception as e:
                    print(f"Error parsing row: {row} - {e}")
                    continue

        # Sort by total points
        leaderboard_data.sort(key=lambda x: x['Total Points'], reverse=True)

        
        for idx, entry in enumerate(leaderboard_data, start=1):
            entry['Rank'] = idx

        return jsonify(leaderboard_data)

    return jsonify({'error': 'Invalid file format'}), 400

@app.route('/')
def home():
    return "GCAF Leaderboard Backend is running!"

if __name__ == '__main__':
    app.run(debug=True)
